Ghazali's Classification of Natural Sciences
Ghazali enumerates the eight principles and seven branches of natural sciences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ghazali classifies the natural sciences into eight principles and seven branches, and why this classification shows that Islamic law does not reject these sciences wholesale.

Core Idea
Ghazali accepts most natural sciences; only four metaphysical claims are disputed.

In this passage, Ghazali begins by stating his intention to list the divisions of the natural sciences to clarify that Islamic law does not require opposing them except in specific places. He then presents a systematic classification of these sciences into eight principles (usul) and seven branches (furu'). This classification is important because it shows that Ghazali and the philosophers share a vast common ground in the empirical sciences.

Guided Path
1
Read the classification list
Read the Arabic passage listing the eight principles and seven branches. Notice the terminology used for each.
The list is divided into two categories.
2
Understand the distinction between principles and branches
Principles are fundamental topics, branches are applied sciences derived from them.
3
Ask: why does Ghazali include souls among the principles?
Reflect on the inclusion of 'souls' as a principle—this is a point where science and philosophy overlap.
This foreshadows the later disputes.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Consider why Ghazali emphasizes that the Law does not reject these sciences. It sets the stage for limited disagreement.
The purpose is to narrow down the actual points of conflict.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الغزالى : لنذكر أقسام هذه العلوم ليعلم أن الشرع ليس يقتضى المنازعة فيها ، ولا إنكارها إلا في مواضع ذكرناها قال : وتنقسم هذه العلوم إلى أصول وفروع : وأصولها ثمانية : الأول : يذكر فيه ما يلحق الجسم من حيث إنه جسم الثاني : يعرف أحوال أقسام أركان العالم الثالث : يعرف أحوال الكون ، والفساد ، والتولد الرابع : فى الأحوال التي تعرض للعناصر الأربعة الخامس : في الجواهر المعدنية السادس : في أحكام النبات السابع : في الحيوانات الثامن : في النفوس أما فروعها فسبعة : الأول : الطب : ومقصوده معرفة مبادئ بدن الإنسان . الثاني : في أحكام النجوم الثالث : علم الفراسة الرابع : التعبير الخامس علم الطلسمات السادس : علم النير نجات السابع علم الكيمياء قال الغزالى : وليس يلزم مخالفتهم شرعاً فى شيء من هذه العلوم، وإنما نخالفهم من جملة هذه العلوم ، في أربع مسائل ، الأولى : حكمهم بأن هذا الاقتران المشاهد في الوجود بين الأسباب والمسببات ، اقتران تلازم بالضرورة . الثانية : قولهم : إن النفوس الإنسانية جواهر قائمة بأنفسها ، ليست منطبقة في الجسم الثالثة : قولهم : إن هذه النفوس يستحيل عليها العدم الرابعة : قولهم : يستحيل رد هذه النفوس إلى الأجساد . قال الغزالى : وإنما يلزم النزاع في مسألة الأسباب والمسببات من حيث إنه يبنى عليها إثبات المعجزات الخارقة للعادة
Al-Ghazali said: Let us mention the divisions of these sciences so that it is known that the Law does not require dispute concerning them, nor denial of them, except in places we have mentioned. He said: And these sciences are divided into principles and branches. Their principles are eight: First: discusses what pertains to the body insofar as it is a body. Second: knows the states of the divisions of the pillars of the world. Third: knows the states of generation, corruption, and reproduction. Fourth: concerning the states that occur to the four elements. Fifth: concerning mineral jewels. Sixth: concerning the judgments of plants. Seventh: concerning animals. Eighth: concerning souls. As for their branches, they are seven: First: Medicine, its purpose is knowledge of the principles of the human body. Second: concerning judgments of the stars. Third: physiognomy. Fourth: dream interpretation. Fifth: the science of talismans. Sixth: the science of al-nayranjāt [?]. Seventh: alchemy. Al-Ghazali said: And it is not necessary to oppose them religiously in any of these sciences. Rather, we oppose them from among these sciences in four issues. The first: their ruling that this observed conjunction in existence between causes and effects is a necessary conjunction. The second: their statement that human souls are self-subsistent substances, not imprinted in the body. The third: their statement that these souls are impossible to perish. The fourth: their statement that it is impossible to return these souls to bodies. Al-Ghazali said: And the dispute concerning the issue of causes and effects is necessary only because upon it is built the establishment of miracles that break the usual course.
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage is a classification followed by an enumeration of points of disagreement. Ghazali begins by stating his intention to list the divisions of the natural sciences so that it is clear that Islamic law does not require disputing or denying them except in specific places. He then divides these sciences into eight principles (usul) and seven branches (furu'). The eight principles cover the body, the cosmic pillars, generation and corruption, the four elements, minerals, plants, animals, and souls. The seven branches are medicine, astrology, physiognomy, dream interpretation, talismans, al-nayranjāt (a type of magic), and alchemy. After listing them, Ghazali asserts that they do not oppose the philosophers religiously in any of these sciences, but rather they oppose them in four specific issues. He enumerates these: (1) the necessary connection between causes and effects, (2) human souls as self-subsistent substances not imprinted in bodies, (3) the impossibility of the annihilation of souls, and (4) the impossibility of returning souls to bodies. Finally, he explains that the dispute about causality is essential because it underlies the affirmation of miracles (breaking the usual course of nature). Thus, Ghazali carefully delimits the scope of theological disagreement with natural philosophy.

Key Terms
الأصول والفروع (al-usul wa al-furu') - principles and branches
الطبيعة (al-tabi'a) - nature

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Ghazali rejects all natural sciences entirely.
Correction: Ghazali explicitly says the Law does not require dispute or denial of these sciences except in specific places, and he lists many that are acceptable.

Checkpoint
How many principles (usul) does Ghazali list for the natural sciences?
A) 6
B) 7
C) 8
D) 9

Key Takeaway
Ghazali's systematic classification shows that he engages with natural sciences and only disputes specific philosophical claims.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Before reading this lesson, did you believe that Ghazali rejected all natural sciences? How does this passage force you to reconsider your assumption about a great scholar? What does that say about your tendency to oversimplify complex figures?
?
This passage shows Ghazali enumerating eight principles and seven branches of natural sciences. Which of these sciences have you dismissed as 'un-Islamic' without proper investigation? What is the cost of such dismissal to your understanding of Islam's engagement with knowledge?
?
Ghazali includes 'souls' among the principles of natural science. How does this challenge your understanding of the relationship between the spiritual and the physical? Do you treat your own soul as a subject of serious study, or do you neglect it in favor of purely material concerns?

The Four Disputed Issues Between Ghazali and the Philosophers
Ghazali lists the four points of theological opposition and highlights causality's role for miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four issues on which Ghazali opposes the philosophers, especially the necessary connection between causes and effects and its relation to miracles.

Core Idea
Only four disputes matter: causality, soul's nature, soul's immortality, and resurrection.

After showing broad agreement, Ghazali now narrows down to four specific points of opposition. These are not minor differences but foundational metaphysical claims about causality, the soul, and the afterlife. He emphasizes that the issue of causality is critical because it underpins the possibility of miracles.

Guided Path
1
Read the four issues list
Read the Arabic passage listing the four issues of disagreement. Note the wording of each.
These are specific philosophical claims.
2
Understand each issue
Identify the core of each: necessary connection between causes and effects, souls as self-subsistent substances, souls cannot perish, souls cannot return to bodies.
These are metaphysical, not empirical.
3
Note the special importance of causality
Ghazali says the dispute about causality is necessary because it underlies miracles. Reflect on why.
Miracles require that the usual causal nexus can be suspended.
4
Ask: why only these four?
Consider why Ghazali limits opposition to these four issues, implying agreement on all other natural sciences.
This reflects his strategy of selective refutation.

Ghazali's Acceptance of the Natural Sciences
Enumeration of natural sciences and Ghazali's acceptance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the classification of natural sciences (al-tabi'iyyat) as presented by Ghazali and his acceptance of them from a religious perspective.

Core Idea
Ghazali does not reject all philosophy; he accepts the natural sciences as tools.

Before diving into Ghazali's critique of the philosophers, it is important to see what he accepts. In this passage, Ghazali lists the main divisions and branches of the natural sciences, showing that his opposition is selective, not total. This sets the stage for his targeted critique.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice how Ghazali first lists the main divisions and then the branches.
The passage is a straightforward classification.
2
Identify the main divisions
There are eight main divisions: from the states of elements to souls. List them in order.
3
Identify the seven branches
Ghazali then lists seven sub-branches: medicine, astrology, physiognomy, dream interpretation, talismans, incantations, alchemy. Note that medicine is given a specific purpose.
4
Notice Ghazali's statement of acceptance
Ghazali explicitly says it is not necessary (laysa yalzam) to oppose them religiously in any of these sciences. This shows his methodological openness.
This is a key nuance often missed.
5
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: why does Ghazali accept these sciences? This acceptance frames his later critique as focused on specific doctrines, not wholesale rejection.
Connects to the broader purpose of the Tahafut.

The seven sub-branches are medicine, astrology, physiognomy, dream interpretation, talismans, incantations (النيرنجات), and alchemy. These four issues form the basis of Ghazali's critique in the subsequent discussions.

?

The Four Points of Disagreement with the Philosophers
Enumeration of four points of disagreement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four specific issues on which Ghazali opposes the philosophers within the natural sciences.

Core Idea
Ghazali's opposition is limited to four core issues about causality, soul, and resurrection.

After accepting the natural sciences, Ghazali narrows his critique to four fundamental issues. These points—causality, the nature of the soul, its immortality, and the possibility of bodily resurrection—are the heart of his disagreement with the philosophers. Understanding them is essential for following the detailed arguments in the Tahafut.

Guided Path
1
Read the four issues
Read the passage listing the four issues. Note the phrasing: 'their judgment that…', 'their statement that…'.
Each issue is a claim attributed to the philosophers.
2
Understand the first issue
The first is about causality: philosophers claim the observed conjunction between causes and effects is necessary (telazum bil-darura). Ghazali will later critique this.
This is the most famous issue.
3
Understand the second issue
The second is about the soul: philosophers claim human souls are self-subsistent substances (jawahir qa'imatan bi-anfusiha) not imprinted in the body.
This relates to the soul's independence from the body.
4
Understand the third and fourth issues
Third: souls cannot perish (al-'adam). Fourth: it is impossible to return these souls to bodies (i.e., bodily resurrection is impossible). Note the contrast with Islamic teachings.
These issues directly challenge Islamic eschatology.
5
Reflect on the selection
Ask: why does Ghazali single out these four? They are the foundations of philosophical doctrines that contradict revelation.
The rest of the Tahafut will refute each.

السادس : علم النيرنجات
السابع : علم الكيمياء
قال الغزالى : وليس يلزم مخالفتهم شرعاً فى شيء من هذه العلوم، وإنما نخالفهم من جملة هذه العلوم ، في أربع مسائل ،
الأولى : حكمهم بأن هذا الاقتران المشاهد في الوجود بين الأسباب والمسببات ، اقتران تلازم بالضرورة .
الثانية : قولهم : إن النفوس الإنسانية جواهر قائمة بأنفسها ، ليست منطبقة في الجسم
الثالثة : قولهم : إن هذه النفوس يستحيل عليها العدم
الرابعة : قولهم : يستحيل رد هذه النفوس إلى الأجساد .
Fourth: on the states that occur to the four elements. Fifth: on mineral jewels. Sixth: on the properties of plants. Seventh: on animals. Eighth: on souls. As for its branches, they are seven: First: medicine: its purpose is knowledge of the principles of the human body. Second: on the judgments of the stars. Third: the science of physiognomy. Fourth: dream interpretation. Fifth: the science of talismans. Sixth: the science of incantations (al-niranjat). Seventh: the science of alchemy. Al-Ghazali said: It is not necessary to oppose them religiously in any of these sciences; we only oppose them from among these sciences in four issues. The first: their judgment that this conjunction observed in existence between causes and effects is a conjunction of necessary correlation. The second: their statement that human souls are self-subsistent substances, not imprinted in the body. The third: their statement that these souls are impossible to perish. The fourth: their statement that it is impossible to return these souls to bodies.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage combines a classification and a statement of disagreement. First, it lists the main divisions and sub-branches of the natural sciences (الطبيعيات) as studied by the philosophers. The main divisions are states of elements, mineral jewels, plants, animals, and souls. The seven sub-branches are medicine, astrology, physiognomy, dream interpretation, talismans, incantations (النيرنجات), and alchemy. Then Ghazali (الغزالى) declares that he does not oppose them in any of these sciences from a shar'i perspective. His opposition is limited to four issues: (1) their claim that the observed conjunction between causes and effects is a necessary correlation; (2) their claim that human souls are self-subsistent substances not imprinted in the body; (3) their claim that these souls are indestructible; and (4) their claim that it is impossible to return these souls to bodies. These four issues form the basis of Ghazali's critique in the subsequent discussions.

تلازم بالضرورة
النفوس الإنسانية
جواهر قائمة بأنفسها
منطبقة
العدم
رد النفوس إلى الأجساد

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many issues does Ghazali oppose the philosophers in?
A) 3
B) 4
C) 5
D) 7

Key Takeaway
Ghazali's critique of philosophy is focused on four key issues: necessary causality, soul's substantiality, its immortality, and the impossibility of bodily resurrection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see events unfold in your life, do you automatically assume the apparent cause was the necessary cause, or do you genuinely pause to recognize that Allah could have willed otherwise? Will you commit to reflecting on Allah's direct involvement in even the smallest occurrences today?
?
Ghazali says the human soul is not imprinted in the body. If your true self is not your physical body, how does that change your attachment to your appearance, health, or even your identity tied to your body? Are you prepared to face death as a release of the soul rather than an end?
?
If bodily resurrection were impossible, would you still feel accountable for your physical actions? Yet Ghazali argues it is both possible and willed by Allah. Do you live today with the certainty that every deed of your body will be resurrected and judged? What one habit will you change to align with that reality?

Ghazali's Objection to Rational Proof of Soul
Ghazali clarifies his objection is against rational proof, not the doctrine itself.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's precise objection to the philosophers' claim about the soul: he does not deny the doctrine but denies that pure reason alone proves it.

Core Idea
Ghazali's objection is epistemological, not theological.

Ghazali begins by clarifying the exact target of his criticism. He is not rejecting the possibility that the soul is a substance, nor does he claim that religious law contradicts this. In fact, he hints that the law confirms it. His objection is specifically to the philosophers' claim that pure reason provides a sufficient proof. This passage sets the stage for his detailed critique of their rational arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice how Ghazali distinguishes between the claim itself and the proof of the claim.
2
Identify Ghazali's two negations
He says he is not objecting as one who thinks the soul's substance is impossible for God, nor as one who thinks the law contradicts it. This shows he accepts the doctrine on religious grounds.
3
Focus on the key phrase 'dallalat mujarrad al-aql'
The denial is specifically about the sufficiency of pure reason. This is the crux of his epistemological critique.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الغزالي : وإنما نريد أن نعترض الآن على دعواهم معرفة كون النفس جوهراً قائماً بنفسه لبراهين العقل ، ولسنا نعترض على دعواهم اعتراض من يبعد ذلك من قدرة الله تعالى ، أو يرى أن الشرع جاء بنقيضه، بل ربما نبين فى تفصيل الحشر والنشر ، أن الشرع مصدق له ، ولكنا ننكر دعواهم دلالة مجرد العقل عليه
Al-Ghazali said: And we only intend now to object to their claim of knowing that the soul is a substance subsisting by itself through rational proofs, and we do not object to their claim as one who deems that far from the power of God, or who sees that the Law has come with its opposite. Rather, perhaps we will explain in the detailing of Resurrection and Gathering that the Law confirms it. But we deny their claim that pure reason indicates it.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage clarifies Al-Ghazali's position in his criticism of the philosophers. He states that his objection is not to the claim that the human soul is a spiritual substance subsisting by itself. He does not reject this as impossible for God, nor does he claim that religious law contradicts it. In fact, he hints that later in discussing Resurrection and Gathering (al-hashr wa al-nashr), he will show that the religious law confirms the soul's subsistence. Instead, his objection is specifically to the philosophers' claim that pure reason alone (mujarrad al-aql) provides a proof for the soul being a substance. Ghazali denies that the rational arguments they offer are sufficient; he does not deny the doctrine itself. Thus, his critique is epistemological, not theological.

Key Terms
النفس جوهر
براهين العقل
مجرد العقل
الحشر والنشر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ghazali denies that the soul is a spiritual substance.
Correction: Ghazali only denies that pure reason proves it; he accepts it based on religious law.

Checkpoint
What does Ghazali say he will explain in the discussion of Resurrection and Gathering?
A) That the soul is mortal
B) That the Law confirms the soul as substance
C) That reason alone suffices
D) That philosophers are wrong

Key Takeaway
Ghazali does not reject the soul's substantiality; he rejects the rational proof of it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What belief do you hold most firmly about yourself or your faith that you have never critically examined the basis of? Are you willing to distinguish between the truth of that belief and the strength of your rational arguments for it, as Ghazali does?
?
Ghazali accepts the soul's substantiality on the basis of revelation (the Law) even while denying rational proof. Is there an area of your life where you demand rational certainty before acting—and is that demand itself a form of epistemic arrogance? What would change if you submitted to revelation in that area?
?
The philosophers placed their confidence in pure reason. Ghazali did not dismiss their conclusion, but he dismantled their proof. If your most cherished convictions were stripped of their rational scaffolding, would your faith collapse, or would it stand on something deeper? What is that something, and how are you cultivating it today?

Method of Learning

Ghazali's Epistemological Challenge
Ghazali states his approach: he objects not to the possibility but to the rational proof of the soul's self-subsistence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's specific methodological intention: he challenges the philosophers' rational proof for the soul's self-subsistence, not the possibility itself.

Core Idea
Ghazali attacks the proof, not the possibility.

Ghazali begins by clarifying his position. He does not reject the idea that the soul is a self-subsistent substance on theological grounds, but rather on epistemic grounds: he demands that the philosophers prove it using reason alone, without relying on revelation. This sets the stage for his critique of their arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let Ghazali's own words come through before you interpret.
Notice how Ghazali distinguishes between what he is not objecting to and what he is objecting to.
2
Identify the two distinctions
Ghazali makes two key distinctions: (1) He does not object because the soul's subsistence is impossible for God or because Sharia contradicts it. (2) He objects to the claim that mere reason can prove it. Find these in the text.
3
Understand the demand for proof
Ghazali demands that the philosophers provide their rational proofs. He acknowledges that they claim many proofs and independence from revelation.
This is the core of his methodology: epistemological critique.
4
Reflect on the implications
Ask yourself: Why does Ghazali make this distinction? What does it say about his approach to philosophy and theology?
It shows he is not rejecting the doctrine itself, but the rational foundation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الغزالي : وإنما نريد أن نعترض الآن على دعواهم معرفة كون النفس جوهراً قائماً بنفسه لبراهين العقل ، ولسنا نعترض على دعواهم اعتراض من يبعد ذلك من قدرة الله تعالى ، أو يرى أن الشرع جاء بنقيضه، بل ربما نبين في تفصيل الحشر والنشر ، أن الشرع مصدق له ، ولكنا ننكر دعواهم دلالة مجرد العقل عليه ، فنطالبهم بالأدلة ، ولهم فيها براهين كثيرة بزعمهم ، والاستغناء عن الشرع فيه
Al-Ghazali said: We only intend now to object to their claim of knowing that the soul is a substance self-subsistent by rational proofs, and we do not object to their claim as one who considers that remote from the power of God Most High, or who sees that the Law has come with its contrary. Rather, perhaps we will explain in the detail of resurrection and gathering that the Law affirms it. But we deny their claim that mere reason indicates it. So we demand of them the proofs, and they have, in their view, many proofs regarding it, and independence from the Law concerning it.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage defines Ghazali's critical stance. He clarifies that he is not objecting to the philosophers' claim that the soul is a self-subsistent substance because it is impossible for God (qadr Allah) or because the sharia contradicts it. In fact, he suggests that the sharia may well affirm it, as he might explain later on the topics of resurrection and gathering (hashr wa nashr). Rather, his objection is epistemological: he denies that mere unaided reason (mujarrad al-`aql) can prove this claim. He therefore demands their proofs, acknowledging that they claim to have many and claim independence from revelation in this matter.

Key Terms
جوهر قائم بنفسه
براهين العقل
قدرة الله
الشرع
الحشر والنشر
مجرد العقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think Ghazali denies the soul's self-subsistence outright, or that he objects on religious grounds.
Correction: Ghazali explicitly says he does not object because it is beyond God's power or because Sharia contradicts it; in fact, Sharia may affirm it. His objection is only to the rational proof.

Checkpoint
What is Ghazali's specific objection to the philosophers' claim about the soul?
A) That it contradicts the sharia
B) That it is impossible for God to create such a soul
C) That their rational proof alone is insufficient
D) That the soul is not a substance

Key Takeaway
Ghazali's critique is epistemological: he denies that unaided reason can prove the soul's self-subsistence, not that the soul is not self-subsistent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When was the last time you held a belief about a hidden matter (like the soul) solely because it 'made sense' to you, without checking what revelation says? How would Ghazali's demand for proof—and his openness to Sharia—challenge that?
?
Ghazali separates the truth of a claim from the strength of its rational proof. Is there a truth you have rejected because you couldn't prove it rationally? What would it take for you to accept it based on another source, like scripture?
?
The philosophers claimed 'independence from the Law.' In what areas of your life do you implicitly claim independence from revelation by relying solely on your own reasoning? Be specific: a decision, a worldview, or a habit.

Ghazali's Defense Against the Charge of Contradiction
Ghazali responds to the charge of contradicting rational principles and reveals the philosophers' error.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ghazali turns the accusation of contradicting rational principles into a demonstration of the philosophers' own logical error.

Core Idea
The apparent contradiction is deliberate—it exposes the philosophers' flawed assumption.

In this passage, a hypothetical critic accuses Ghazali of contradicting rational principles by questioning a seemingly airtight proof. Ghazali responds by reframing the contradiction as evidence of the philosophers' oversight. This lesson unpacks his method and the hidden assumption that caused the confusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Start by reading the critic's claim: the two premises are indubitable, so the conclusion must be accepted. Notice how they accuse Ghazali of inconsistency.
The critic assumes that rational principles are beyond dispute.
2
Examine Ghazali's reply
Ghazali states that his book's purpose is to expose incoherence. He then identifies the real flaw: the philosophers' assumption that knowledge is like a color impressed in the body.
3
Identify the point of confusion
Focus on the phrase 'موضع التلبيس' (point of obfuscation). Ghazali pinpoints the false analogy between knowledge and color as the source of error.
This analogy leads to the false conclusion that the soul is divisible.
4
Reflect on Ghazali's method
Consider why Ghazali frames his project as 'بيان التهافت والتناقض'. How does this response fit his overall strategy in Tahafut?
He is not rejecting rational principles, but showing where the philosophers misapplied them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الغزالي : فإن قيل : هذه مناقضة في المعقولات ، والمعقولات لا تنقض ؛ فإنكم مهما لم تقدروا على الشك في المقدمتين وهو أن العلم الواحد لا ينقسم ، وأن ما لا ينقسم لا يقوم بجسم منقسم ، لم يمكنكم الشك في النتيجة قلنا : إن هذا الكتاب ما صنفناه إلا لبيان التهافت والتناقض في كلام الفلاسفة وقد حصل ثم نقول : هذه المناقضة تبين أنهم غفلوا عن موضع تلبيس في القياس ، ولعل موضع الالتباس قولهم : إن العلم منطبع في الجسم ، انطباع اللون في محله ، فينقسم العلم بانقسام الجسم مثل ما ينقسم اللون بانقسام محله
Al-Ghazali said: If it is said: This is a contradiction in rational matters, and rational matters are not contradictory; for as long as you are unable to doubt the two premises—that one knowledge is indivisible, and that what is indivisible does not subsist in a divisible body—you cannot doubt the conclusion. We say: This book was not authored by us except to show the incoherence and contradiction in the speech of the philosophers, and it has been achieved. Then we say: This contradiction shows that they neglected a point of obfuscation in the syllogism, and perhaps the point of confusion is their saying: Knowledge is impressed in the body, like the impression of color in its place, so knowledge is divided by the division of the body just as color is divided by the division of its place.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage contains an objection-answer pair. A hypothetical objector says: 'This is a contradiction in rational matters (munāqaḍa fī al-ma`qūlāt), but rational matters cannot be contradictory. Since you cannot doubt the two premises (that a single knowledge is indivisible, and that what is indivisible cannot subsist in a divisible body), you cannot doubt the conclusion that the soul is indivisible. Thus your objection contradicts reason itself.' Ghazali replies that the very purpose of his book (Tahafut al-Falasifa) is to expose the incoherence and contradiction (al-tahāfut wa al-tanāquḍ) in the philosophers' statements. So finding a contradiction in their reasoning is exactly what he intends. Then he adds that the apparent contradiction actually reveals their negligence: they falsely assume that knowledge is 'impressed' in the body like a color in its substrate, so that it divides with the body's division. This assumption is the source of confusion (al-talbīs) in their syllogism.

Key Terms
مناقضة
المعقولات
المقدمتين
النتيجة
بيان التهافت والتناقض
انطباع العلم
موضع التلبيس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think Ghazali is committing a logical fallacy or denying rational principles.
Correction: Ghazali clarifies that exposing the philosophers' own contradiction is his method, not an error. He is not rejecting rational principles but showing their misapplication.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, what is the source of the philosophers' confusion in the first proof?
A) They deny the existence of indivisible substances
B) They assume knowledge is impressed in the body like color
C) They fail to distinguish between rational and revealed knowledge
D) They ignore the role of the estimative power

Key Takeaway
Ghazali's method is to uncover the hidden assumptions in the philosophers' syllogisms, turning their own accusations of contradiction into evidence of their error.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a belief or argument that seems to contradict your faith, do you immediately dismiss it as false, or do you take the time to examine the hidden assumptions behind it? Ghazali’s example shows that apparent contradictions can reveal deeper errors. What assumption in your own life might be causing you to reject truth you need to accept?
?
The philosophers assumed knowledge is like a physical object—divisible and impressed in matter. Are there ways you have reduced spiritual realities (like faith, intention, or love for God) to material or mechanical processes? How might that be distorting your relationship with Allah?
?
Ghazali wrote this entire book to expose the incoherence of flawed thinking. Is there an area of your life where you have avoided critical self-examination because it would be uncomfortable? Will you commit today to honestly review one belief or practice that you have never questioned?
